     Plan: Migrate VoiceMode from Whisper/Kokoro to ElevenLabs

     Context

     VoiceMode currently uses Whisper.cpp (local) and OpenAI Whisper API (cloud)
      for STT, and Kokoro (local) and OpenAI TTS (cloud) for TTS. All providers
     expose OpenAI-compatible endpoints (/v1/audio/transcriptions and
     /v1/audio/speech) via AsyncOpenAI clients.

     Goal: Make ElevenLabs the default and primary provider for both STT and
     TTS:
     - STT: ElevenLabs Scribe v2 Realtime (WebSocket streaming, ~150ms latency)
     - TTS: ElevenLabs eleven_flash_v2_5 (~75ms latency)

     Whisper/Kokoro code stays for fallback but ElevenLabs is the default when
     ELEVENLABS_API_KEY is set.

     User Preferences

     - API Key: sk_6ce522e9173eb1395f4bd34d726b38b3c79750fa7063d9c6
     - Default Voice ID: k4hP4cQadSZQc0Oar2Ld
     - Default TTS Model: eleven_flash_v2_5
     - STT Model: scribe_v2_realtime (realtime streaming)
     - Strategy: ElevenLabs replaces Whisper/Kokoro as default

     Current Architecture

     Mic ‚Üí record_audio_with_silence_detection() ‚Üí numpy array (full recording)
       ‚Üí prepare_audio_for_stt() ‚Üí compressed file (mp3/wav)
       ‚Üí simple_stt_failover() ‚Üí AsyncOpenAI.audio.transcriptions.create()
       ‚Üí text result

     Text ‚Üí simple_tts_failover() ‚Üí core.text_to_speech()
       ‚Üí AsyncOpenAI.audio.speech.create() ‚Üí audio stream
       ‚Üí NonBlockingAudioPlayer ‚Üí speaker

     Key Insight: Realtime STT Changes the Recording Model

     Currently: Record full audio ‚Üí stop ‚Üí compress ‚Üí upload ‚Üí wait for
     transcription.
     With Scribe v2 Realtime: Stream audio chunks via WebSocket ‚Üí get
     partial/committed transcripts live ‚Üí done when silence detected (VAD on
     server side).

     This means we can bypass the local VAD + record-then-transcribe pattern
     entirely for ElevenLabs, getting much lower latency.

     Files to Modify

     ‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź

     Implementation Steps

     Step 1: Add dependency

     File: pyproject.toml

     Add elevenlabs>=1.0.0 to dependencies.

     Step 2: Create ElevenLabs client wrapper

     New file: voice_mode/elevenlabs_client.py

     from elevenlabs import ElevenLabs
     from typing import Optional, Iterator
     import logging

     logger = logging.getLogger("voicemode")

     _client: Optional[ElevenLabs] = None

     def get_client(api_key: str) -> ElevenLabs:
         """Get or create singleton ElevenLabs client."""
         global _client
         if _client is None:
             _client = ElevenLabs(api_key=api_key)
         return _client

     async def elevenlabs_tts(
         text: str,
         voice_id: str,
         model_id: str = "eleven_flash_v2_5",
         output_format: str = "pcm_24000",
         speed: float = 1.0,
         api_key: str = "",
     ) -> Iterator[bytes]:
         """Generate speech using ElevenLabs TTS (streaming)."""
         client = get_client(api_key)
         return client.text_to_speech.stream(
             text=text,
             voice_id=voice_id,
             model_id=model_id,
             output_format=output_format,
             voice_settings={"speed": speed} if speed != 1.0 else None,
         )

     async def elevenlabs_stt_batch(
         audio_file,
         model_id: str = "scribe_v2",
         language_code: Optional[str] = None,
         keyterms: Optional[list] = None,
         api_key: str = "",
     ) -> dict:
         """Transcribe audio using ElevenLabs Scribe v2 (batch)."""
         client = get_client(api_key)
         kwargs = {"file": audio_file, "model_id": model_id}
         if language_code and language_code != "auto":
             kwargs["language_code"] = language_code
         if keyterms:
             kwargs["keyterms"] = keyterms
         result = client.speech_to_text.convert(**kwargs)
         return {"text": result.text, "language": getattr(result,
     "language_code", None)}

     Step 3: Create Realtime STT module

     New file: voice_mode/elevenlabs_realtime_stt.py

     This is the core architectural addition. Instead of record ‚Üí compress ‚Üí
     upload:

     import asyncio
     import numpy as np
     import sounddevice as sd
     from elevenlabs import ElevenLabs
     from typing import Optional, Callable
     import logging

     logger = logging.getLogger("voicemode")

     async def realtime_transcribe(
         api_key: str,
         max_duration: float = 120.0,
         min_duration: float = 2.0,
         language_code: Optional[str] = None,
         keyterms: Optional[list] = None,
         on_partial: Optional[Callable] = None,  # For future live feedback
     ) -> Optional[dict]:
         """
         Stream microphone audio to ElevenLabs Scribe v2 Realtime via WebSocket.

         Uses server-side VAD to auto-commit when silence is detected.
         Returns committed transcript text.

         Flow:
         1. Open WebSocket connection to Scribe v2 Realtime
         2. Start recording from microphone
         3. Stream audio chunks (PCM 16kHz) to WebSocket
         4. Receive partial_transcript events (optional live feedback)
         5. On committed_transcript event (VAD silence), stop and return text
         6. Respect max_duration timeout
         """
         client = ElevenLabs(api_key=api_key)
         committed_text = ""

         async with client.speech_to_text.realtime.connect(
             model_id="scribe_v2_realtime",
             language_code=language_code if language_code and language_code !=
     "auto" else None,
             # VAD auto-commit for mic input
         ) as connection:
             # Set up audio streaming from microphone
             sample_rate = 16000  # Scribe expects 16kHz
             chunk_duration_ms = 100  # 100ms chunks
             chunk_samples = int(sample_rate * chunk_duration_ms / 1000)

             recording = True
             start_time = asyncio.get_event_loop().time()

             async def stream_mic():
                 """Stream microphone audio chunks to the WebSocket."""
                 nonlocal recording
                 loop = asyncio.get_event_loop()

                 with sd.InputStream(
                     samplerate=sample_rate,
                     channels=1,
                     dtype='int16',
                     blocksize=chunk_samples,
                 ) as stream:
                     while recording:
                         elapsed = loop.time() - start_time
                         if elapsed >= max_duration:
                             recording = False
                             break

                         # Read audio chunk
                         data, overflowed = stream.read(chunk_samples)
                         if overflowed:
                             logger.warning("Audio buffer overflow")

                         # Send PCM bytes to WebSocket
                         await connection.send_audio(data.tobytes())
                         await asyncio.sleep(chunk_duration_ms / 1000 * 0.8)

             # Start mic streaming in background
             mic_task = asyncio.create_task(stream_mic())

             try:
                 # Listen for transcription events
                 async for event in connection:
                     if event.type == "partial_transcript":
                         if on_partial:
                             on_partial(event.text)
                     elif event.type == "committed_transcript":
                         committed_text = event.text
                         elapsed = asyncio.get_event_loop().time() - start_time
                         if elapsed >= min_duration and committed_text.strip():
                             # Got a committed transcript after min duration
                             recording = False
                             break
             finally:
                 recording = False
                 mic_task.cancel()
                 try:
                     await mic_task
                 except asyncio.CancelledError:
                     pass

         if committed_text.strip():
             return {
                 "text": committed_text.strip(),
                 "provider": "elevenlabs",
                 "endpoint": "scribe_v2_realtime",
                 "metrics": {"is_local": False}
             }
         else:
             return {"error_type": "no_speech", "provider": "elevenlabs"}

  Here's a summary of everything implemented:

  Summary of Changes

  New Files

  1. voice_mode/elevenlabs_client.py - ElevenLabs SDK wrapper with
  elevenlabs_tts_stream(), elevenlabs_tts_convert(), and elevenlabs_stt_batch()
  2. voice_mode/elevenlabs_realtime_stt.py - Realtime WebSocket STT using Scribe
   v2 Realtime with server-side VAD, streams mic audio directly

  Modified Files

  3. pyproject.toml - Added elevenlabs>=1.0.0 dependency
  4. voice_mode/config.py - Added ELEVENLABS_API_KEY, ELEVENLABS_TTS_MODEL,
  ELEVENLABS_TTS_VOICE, ELEVENLABS_STT_MODEL, ELEVENLABS_USE_REALTIME_STT config
   vars. Auto-prepends ElevenLabs as primary provider when API key is set. Added
   config template docs.
  5. voice_mode/provider_discovery.py - Added "elevenlabs" provider type
  detection and registry initialization for ElevenLabs TTS/STT endpoints
  6. voice_mode/simple_failover.py - Added ElevenLabs TTS branch (streaming PCM
  playback) and batch STT branch in failover chains
  7. voice_mode/tools/converse.py - Added realtime STT path that bypasses
  record-then-transcribe when ElevenLabs is configured, falling back to
  traditional path otherwise
  8. voice_mode/providers.py - Updated voice routing to prefer ElevenLabs when
  configured, added ElevenLabs to provider maps

  How It Works

  - When ELEVENLABS_API_KEY is set, ElevenLabs becomes the primary provider for
  both TTS and STT
  - TTS: Streams PCM audio from ElevenLabs eleven_flash_v2_5 (~75ms latency) ‚Üí
  plays via NonBlockingAudioPlayer
  - STT: Uses Scribe v2 Realtime WebSocket with server-side VAD ‚ÄĒ streams mic
  audio directly, bypassing local recording + compression
  - Failover: If ElevenLabs fails, falls back to Kokoro/Whisper (local) ‚Üí OpenAI
   (cloud)
  - All existing Whisper/Kokoro/OpenAI code remains functional

  - TTS Model: eleven_flash_v2_5 (~75ms latency)
  - STT Model: scribe_v2_realtime (streaming)

  fails, it falls back to your existing Whisper/Kokoro/OpenAI providers.

  Now let me explain the Claude Desktop Cowork setup:

  How to Use VoiceMode

  1. Claude Code (CLI) - Already Set Up

  VoiceMode is already configured as an MCP server. Just use /voicemode:converse
   or the converse MCP tool.

  2. Claude Desktop / Cowork

  Add to your Claude Desktop MCP config (~/Library/Application 
  Support/Claude/claude_desktop_config.json):

  {
    "mcpServers": {
      "voicemode": {
        "command": "uvx",
        "args": ["voice-mode"],
        "env": {
          "ELEVENLABS_API_KEY":
  "sk_6ce522e9173eb1395f4bd34d726b38b3c79750fa7063d9c6"
        }
      }
    }
  }

  3. Factory Droid

  The plugin is now in .factory/. To use it:

  # Option A: Install from this repo's .factory directory
  droid plugin install voicemode

  # Option B: Add MCP server to Droid config
  # In ~/.factory/mcp.json:
  {
    "mcpServers": {
      "voicemode": {
        "command": "uvx",
        "args": ["voice-mode"],
        "env": {
          "ELEVENLABS_API_KEY":
  "sk_6ce522e9173eb1395f4bd34d726b38b3c79750fa7063d9c6"
        }
      }
    }
  }

  Summary of what was done:

‚Źļ Found it. Line 110-111: the player converts to float32, but it doesn't 
  normalize. When you have int16 data (range -32768 to 32767) and cast it to
  float32 without dividing by 32768, the values are thousands instead of -1.0 to
   1.0. That's why it sounds like a war zone ‚ÄĒ the audio is massively
  clipped/distorted.

  Let me fix the PCM conversion:

‚ĚĮ oh you sweet dumb cunt > ## Documentation Index                               
> Fetch the complete documentation index at: https://docs.factory.ai/llms.txt   
> Use this file to discover all available pages before exploring further.       
                                                                                
# Plugins                                                                       
                                                                                
> Extend Droid with shareable packages of skills, commands, and tools.          
                                                                                
Plugins let you extend Droid with custom functionality that can be shared       
across projects and teams. A plugin bundles skills, slash commands, agents, and 
 MCP servers into a single, distributable package.                              
                                                                                
## What are plugins?                                                            
                                                                                
Plugins are directories containing a manifest file                              
(`.factory-plugin/plugin.json`) and optional components like skills, commands,  
and agents. Unlike standalone configuration in `.factory/`, plugins are         
designed for sharing and distribution.                                          
                                                                                
**Plugin components:**                                                          
                                                                                
| Component       | Purpose                                           |         
Invocation                                |                                     
| --------------- | ------------------------------------------------- |         
----------------------------------------- |                                     
| **Skills**      | Reusable capabilities with instructions and tools |         
Model-invoked automatically based on task |                                     
| **Commands**    | Slash commands for specific workflows             |         
User-invoked via `/command-name`          |                                     
| **Agents**      | Specialized subagent definitions                  | Called  
via Task tool                      |                                            
| **Hooks**       | Lifecycle event handlers                          |         
Automatic on matching events              |                                     
| **MCP Servers** | External tool integrations                        |         
Available as tools when plugin is active  |                                     
                                                                                
## When to use plugins vs standalone configuration                              
                                                                                
| Approach                               | Best for                             
                                                            |                   
| -------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------ 
----------------------------------------------------------- |                   
| **Standalone** (`.factory/` directory) | Personal workflows, project-specific 
 customizations, quick experiments                          |                   
| **Plugins**                            | Sharing with teammates, distributing 
 to community, versioned releases, reusable across projects |                   
                                                                                
Start with standalone configuration in `.factory/` for quick iteration, then    
convert to a plugin when you're ready to share.                                 
                                                                                
## Managing plugins                                                             
                                                                                
Droid provides two ways to manage plugins:                                      
                                                                                
### Interactive UI (recommended)                                                
                                                                                
Use the `/plugins` slash command to open the plugin manager:                    
                                                                                
```                                                                             
/p                                                                              
‚Ä¶ +221 lines ‚Ä¶                                                                  
------------------------------------------------------------------ |            
| **droid-evolved**     | Skills for continuous learning: session navigation,   
human writing, skill creation, visual design, frontend design, browser          
automation |                                                                    
| **security-engineer** | Security review, threat modeling, commit scanning,    
and vulnerability validation                                                    
    |                                                                           
                                                                                
Install via `/plugins` UI (Browse tab) or CLI:                                  
                                                                                
```bash  theme={null}                                                           
droid plugin install droid-evolved@factory-plugins                              
droid plugin install security-engineer@factory-plugins                          
```

### Enterprise Plugin Registry                                                  
                                                                                
For organizations that need centralized control over approved plugins, see      
[Enterprise Plugin Registry](/enterprise/enterprise-plugin-registry). This      
allows you to:                                                                  
                                                                                
* Maintain a private marketplace of approved plugins                            
* Pre-install mandatory plugins for all users                                   
* Organize plugins by team, role, or capability                                 
                                                                                
### Claude Code compatibility                                                   
                                                                                
Droid is compatible with plugins built for Claude Code. If you find a Claude    
Code plugin you'd like to use, you can install it directly - the plugin format  
is interoperable. See the [Claude Code plugins                                  
documentation](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/plugins) for more details.

       22 +## Parameters                                                 
       23 +                                                              
       24 +| Parameter | Default | Description |                         
       25 +|-----------|---------|-------------|                         
       26 +| `message` | required | Text to speak to the user |          
       27 +| `wait_for_response` | `true` | Whether to listen after speak
          +ing. Set `false` for announcements/narration. |               
       28 +| `listen_duration_max` | `120` | Maximum seconds to listen be
          +fore stopping |                                               
       29 +| `listen_duration_min` | `2.0` | Minimum seconds before silen
          +ce detection can trigger. Increase if user gets cut off. |    
       30 +| `disable_silence_detection` | `false` | Set `true` to record
          + for the full `listen_duration_max` without auto-stopping. |  
       31 +| `vad_aggressiveness` | `3` | Voice Activity Detection strict
          +ness (0-3). 3 = most strict (stops quickly on silence). Lower 
          +values = more tolerant of pauses. |                           
       32 +| `wait_for_conch` | `false` | If another agent is already spe
          +aking, `false` returns immediately. `true` waits until the oth
          +er agent finishes, then speaks. |                             
       33 +                                                              
       34 +## Common Patterns                                            
       35 +                                                              
       36 +### Speak and listen (default)                                
       37 +```python                                                     
       38 +voicemode:converse("What would you like to work on?")         
       39 +```                                                           
       40 +                                                              
       41 +### Announce without listening (narration)                    
       42 +```python                                                     
       43 +voicemode:converse("Searching the codebase now...", wait_for_r
          +esponse=false)                                                
       44 +```                                                           
       45 +                                                              
       46 +### Long response expected (user gives detailed instructions) 
       47 +```python                                                     
       48 +voicemode:converse("Go ahead, I'm listening.", listen_duration
          +_max=120, listen_duration_min=5, disable_silence_detection=tru
          +e)                                                            
       49 +```                                                           
       50 +                                                              
       51 +### User keeps getting cut off (increase min duration)        
       52 +```python                                                     
       53 +voicemode:converse("Take your time.", listen_duration_min=10, 
          +vad_aggressiveness=1)                                         
       54 +```                                                           
       55 +                                                              
       56 +### Parallel: speak while doing work                          
       57 +```python                                                     
       58 +# These run simultaneously - no dead air                      
       59 +voicemode:converse("Checking that now.", wait_for_response=fal
          +se)                                                           
       60 +bash("git status")                                            
       61 +```                                                           
       62 +                                                              
       63 +### Queue behind another speaker                              
       64 +```python                                                     
       65 +voicemode:converse("My turn to speak.", wait_for_conch=true)  
       66 +```                                                           
       67 +                                                              
       68 +## Silence Detection                                          
       69 +                                                              
       70 +By default, the tool uses WebRTC VAD (Voice Activity Detection
          +) to automatically stop recording when the user stops speaking
          +.                                                             
       71 +                                                              
       72 +- **VAD aggressiveness 3** (default): Stops after ~1 second of
          + silence. Good for quick responses.                           
       73 +- **VAD aggressiveness 0**: Very tolerant of pauses. Good for 
          +users who think while speaking.                               
       74 +- **disable_silence_detection=true**: Records for the full `li
          +sten_duration_max`. Use when the user needs to give long instr
          +uctions.                                                      
       75 +                                                              
       76 +## When the User Gets Cut Off                                 
       77 +                                                              
       78 +If the user reports being cut off mid-sentence:               
       79 +1. Increase `listen_duration_min` to 5-10 seconds             
       80 +2. Lower `vad_aggressiveness` to 1 or 2                       
       81 +3. Or set `disable_silence_detection=true` with a reasonable `
          +listen_duration_max`                                          
       82 +                                                              
       83 +## Conch (Multi-Agent)                                        
       84 +                                                              
       85 +Only one agent can use the microphone at a time. The "conch" i
          +s a lock that prevents overlapping conversations.             
       86 +

‚Źļ Now I see the critical issues. Let me read our implementation to
  cross-reference:

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

‚Źļ Now I have the full picture. Here's the cross-reference analysis:

  Issues Found

  Issue 1: stream() uses mpv which expects MP3, but we don't specify 
  output_format

  SDK source (play.py:69-97): The stream() function pipes raw bytes to mpv 
  --no-cache. mpv auto-detects format from the byte stream.

  Our code (elevenlabs_tts_stt.py:48): el_client.text_to_speech.stream() without
   output_format ‚ÄĒ the default output format from ElevenLabs API is
  mp3_44100_128.

  The "war sounds" issue: When we had output_format="pcm_24000" earlier, mpv was
   receiving raw PCM bytes with no header ‚ÄĒ it couldn't detect the format, so it
   played garbage. The current code doesn't specify format (defaults to MP3),
  which should work. But eleven_v3 may return a different default format or have
   different streaming behavior.

  Fix: Explicitly set output_format="mp3_44100_128" to guarantee mpv gets MP3.

  Issue 2: play() vs stream() ‚ÄĒ different functions

  SDK: play() collects ALL bytes first then plays via ffplay. stream() pipes
  chunks to mpv as they arrive.

  For eleven_v3: If the model streams differently or the first chunks don't
  contain valid MP3 header data, mpv can choke. The play() function would be
  safer since it collects everything first.

  Fix: For eleven_v3, use convert() + play() instead of stream().

  Issue 3: STT example uses scribe_v2 ‚ÄĒ our code matches correctly

  No issue here.

  Issue 4: Conversational AI example is dead simple

  The demo.py shows the entire Conversational AI integration is just ~20 lines
  of code. No custom audio handling needed.

  Issue 5: WHISPER_LANGUAGE variable name is confusing

  We import WHISPER_LANGUAGE for ElevenLabs STT. Should be renamed to something
  generic.

  Issue 6: Speed default 1.0, not 1.2

  The linter changed it from our desired 1.2 to 1.0. Need to set it back.

  Let me fix the critical TTS issues now:

‚Źļ Update(voice_mode/elevenlabs_tts_stt.py)

‚Źļ Let me look at how the SDK's realtime STT actually works, then fix our
  implementation.

  Read 2 files (ctrl+o to expand)

‚Źļ Now I fully understand the SDK. Our elevenlabs_realtime_stt.py was using the
  wrong API patterns. The SDK uses:

  1. connect() takes a dict, not keyword args wrapped in RealtimeAudioOptions()
  2. Event handlers use connection.on(RealtimeEvents.X, callback) ‚ÄĒ callbacks
  receive the raw data dict
  3. Audio is sent as {"audio_base_64": base64_chunk} via connection.send()
  4. With CommitStrategy.VAD, commits happen server-side automatically
  5. The data dict has "text" key directly (no .text attribute)

  Let me rewrite the realtime STT module properly:

connect_status                                                                  
  voicemode                                                                     
                                                                                
  Tool name: connect_status                                                     
  Full name: mcp__voicemode__connect_status                                     
                                                                                
  Description:                                                                  
  VoiceMode Connect status and presence.                                        
                                                                                
  Check connection status and who's online, or set your availability.           
  Idempotent ‚ÄĒ safe to call multiple times. Creates user if needed.             
                                                                                
  Args:                                                                         
      set_presence: Optional. Set to "available" (green dot - ready for calls)  
          or "away" (amber dot - connected but not accepting calls).            
          Omit to just check status.                                            
          Note: "available" requires wake-from-idle capability. In Claude Code, 
          create a team first (TeamCreate) to enable this. Without a team,      
          presence is downgraded to "away" with guidance on how to enable it.   
      username: Optional. Your Connect username (e.g., "cora", "astrid").       
          Used to identify which user to register on this WebSocket.            
          The PostToolUse hook provides this in its systemMessage.              
                                                                                
  Returns:                                                                      
      Connection status, online contacts, and presence state.                   
                                                                                
  Examples:                                                                     
      connect_status()                                         # Check status   
      connect_status(set_presence="available", username="cora") # Go available  
      connect_status(set_presence="away")                       # Go away       
                                                                                
  Parameters:                                                                   
    ‚ÄĘ set_presence: unknown                                                     
    ‚ÄĘ username: unknown                                                         
converse                                                                        
  voicemode                                                                     
                                                                                
  Tool name: converse                                                           
  Full name: mcp__voicemode__converse                                           
                                                                                
  Description:                                                                  
  Have an ongoing voice conversation - speak a message and optionally listen    
for response.                                                                   
                                                                                
  <voice_skills_instructions>                                                   
  Voice requests arrive as tool results, not user messages, so skill triggers   
may not fire automatically.                                                     
                                                                                
  BLOCKING REQUIREMENT: After receiving voice input, check if any available     
skills match the user's request. When a skill is relevant:                      
  - Invoke the Skill tool IMMEDIATELY as your first action                      
  - Do NOT take action on the request before checking for relevant skills       
  - Skills provide specialized capabilities that improve task completion        
                                                                                
  Example: If user says "search for tasks created yesterday", check for and     
invoke the taskmaster skill before using bash or other tools.                   
  </voice_skills_instructions>                                                  
                                                                                
                                                                                
  ūüĒĆ ENDPOINT: STT/TTS services must expose OpenAI-compatible endpoints:        
     /v1/audio/transcriptions and /v1/audio/speech                              
                                                                                
  ūüďö DOCUMENTATION: See MCP resources for detailed information:                 
     - voicemode://docs/quickstart - Basic usage and common examples            
     - voicemode://docs/parameters - Complete parameter reference               
     - voicemode://docs/languages - Non-English language support guide          
     - voicemode://docs/patterns - Best practices and conversation patterns     
     - voicemode://docs/troubleshooting - Audio, VAD, and connectivity issues   
                                                                                
  KEY PARAMETERS:                                                               
  ‚ÄĘ message (required): The message to speak                                    
  ‚ÄĘ wait_for_response (bool, default: true): Listen for response after speaking 
  ‚ÄĘ voice (string): TTS voice name (auto-selected unless specified)             
  ‚ÄĘ tts_provider ("openai"|"kokoro"): Provider selection (auto-selected unless  
specified)                                                                      
  ‚ÄĘ disable_silence_detection (bool, default: false): Disable auto-stop on      
silence                                                                         
  ‚ÄĘ vad_aggressiveness (0-3, default: 3): Voice detection strictness            
(0=permissive, 3=strict)                                                        
  ‚ÄĘ speed (0.25-4.0): Speech rate (1.0=normal, 2.0=double speed)                
  ‚ÄĘ chime_enabled (bool): Enable/disable audio feedback chimes                  
  ‚ÄĘ chime_leading_silence (float): Silence before chime in seconds              
  ‚ÄĘ chime_trailing_silence (float): Silence after chime in seconds              
  ‚ÄĘ metrics_level ("minimal"|"summary"|"verbose"): Output detail level          
    - minimal: Just response text (saves tokens)                                
    - summary: Response + compact timing (default)                              
    - verbose: Response + detailed metrics breakdown                            
  ‚ÄĘ wait_for_conch (bool, default: false): Multi-agent coordination             
    - false: If another agent is speaking, return status immediately            
    - true: Wait until the other agent finishes, then speak                     
                                                                                
  TIMING PARAMETERS (usually leave at defaults):                                
    Silence detection handles most cases automatically. Only override these if  
    silence detection is disabled or the user reports being cut off.            
    Defaults are configurable by the user via ~/.voicemode/voicemode.env.       
  ‚ÄĘ listen_duration_max (number, default: 120): Max listen time in seconds      
  ‚ÄĘ listen_duration_min (number, default: 2.0): Min recording time before       
silence detection                                                               
                                                                                
  PRIVACY: Microphone access required when wait_for_response=true.              
           Audio processed via STT service, not stored.                         
                                                                                
  RECOGNITION TIP: If specific words are consistently misrecognized, configure  
     VOICEMODE_STT_PROMPT for vocabulary biasing - see                          
voicemode://docs/parameters                                                     
                                                                                
  For complete parameter list, advanced options, and detailed examples,         
  consult the MCP resources listed above.                                       
                                                                                
                                                                                
  Parameters:                                                                   
    ‚ÄĘ message (required): string                                                
    ‚ÄĘ wait_for_response: unknown                                                
    ‚ÄĘ listen_duration_max: number                                               
    ‚ÄĘ listen_duration_min: number                                               
    ‚ÄĘ timeout: number                                                           
    ‚ÄĘ voice: unknown                                                            
    ‚ÄĘ tts_provider: unknown                                                     
    ‚ÄĘ tts_model: unknown                                                        
    ‚ÄĘ tts_instructions: unknown                                                 
    ‚ÄĘ chime_enabled: unknown

‚ĚĮ ok now this is my final v1 dfeature request before we lock this and proceed

‚Źļ Good question. Let me explain the current architecture first, then the remote
  server approach.

  Current Architecture (per-client server)

  Client (Claude Code / Droid)
    ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ spawns: uvx voicemode (stdio MCP server)
          ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ runs locally on YOUR machine
                ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ TTS: ElevenLabs API ‚Üí audio bytes ‚Üí ffplay (plays on YOUR
  speakers)
                ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ STT: YOUR microphone ‚Üí sounddevice ‚Üí audio bytes ‚Üí
  ElevenLabs API
                ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ The MCP server MUST run on the same machine as mic/speakers

  Why it's per-client: The server directly accesses your hardware (microphone
  via sounddevice, speakers via ffplay). These are OS-level resources that
  require the process to be running on the same machine.

  Remote Server Architecture (what you're asking)

  Your Machine (single server)
    ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ voicemode serve (HTTP MCP server on port 8765)
          ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ TTS: ElevenLabs API ‚Üí audio ‚Üí ffplay (YOUR speakers)
          ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ STT: YOUR microphone ‚Üí sounddevice ‚Üí ElevenLabs API
          ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ Exposes: Streamable HTTP at http://localhost:8765/mcp

  Client 1 (Claude Code)  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ HTTP ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź
  Client 2 (Droid)         ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ HTTP ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Üí http://localhost:8765/mcp
  Client 3 (claude.ai)     ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ HTTP ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

  This already exists. VoiceMode has a voicemode serve command that starts an
  HTTP MCP server. The audio I/O still happens on your machine (where the server
   runs), but clients connect over HTTP instead of each spawning their own
  server.

  Let me check the current serve implementation:

  Searched for 1 pattern (ctrl+o to expand)

‚Źļ It already exists. Here's the setup:

  What You Need to Do

  Step 1: Start the server once on your machine:
  voicemode serve
  # Starts HTTP MCP server at http://127.0.0.1:8765/mcp
  # Transport: streamable-http

  Step 2: Point ALL clients to it instead of uvx:

  {
    "mcpServers": {
      "voicemode": {
        "type": "url",
        "url": "http://127.0.0.1:8765/mcp"
      }
    }
  }

  No uvx, no uv run, no spawning a new Python process per client. One server,
  all clients connect over HTTP.

  Network & I/O Architecture

  Key Points

  - Audio I/O is always on the server machine ‚ÄĒ mic and speakers are hardware,
  can't be remoted over HTTP
  - ElevenLabs API calls happen server-side ‚ÄĒ one API key, one connection
  - Clients only send/receive JSON ‚ÄĒ MCP tool calls over HTTP, no audio data
  flows to clients
  - One process, multiple clients ‚ÄĒ no duplicate Python environments

  localhost:8765 and set up the serve command to auto-start?

‚Źļ voicemode - converse (MCP)(message: "Good question. There are two transport
                            modes in MCP. Stdio mode means the client spawns the
                             server as a child process. The client and server
                            talk through stdin and stdout pipes. No network, no
                            ports, no HTTP. It's the simplest setup because the
                            client manages the server lifecycle. That's the uvx
                            approach. Each client starts its own voicemode
                            process. The HTTP mode means you run the server
                            yourself, separately. It listens on a port. Clients
                            connect over HTTP. The server stays running even
                            when clients disconnect. The original VoiceMode was
                            designed for stdio because that's how most MCP
                            servers work in Claude Code. The HTTP serve mode was
                             added later for remote access scenarios. For your
                            use case with multiple clients, HTTP is clearly
                            better. One server, one process, one set of
                            dependencies. Let me update the MCP configs and the
                            plugin to use HTTP mode. I'll also set up auto-start
                             so the server launches on login.",
                            wait_for_response: "true", speed: 1.2,
                            listen_duration_min: 5)

     Plan: VoiceMode v2 ‚ÄĒ HTTP Remote Server + Tech Debt Reconciliation

     Context

     VoiceMode v1 runs as a stdio MCP server spawned per-client via uvx. Every
     client (Claude Code, Factory Droid) starts its own Python process. This
     wastes resources and means code changes require cache-busting (--refresh).

     Goal: Run VoiceMode as a single persistent HTTP server on the user's
     machine. All clients connect to http://localhost:8765/mcp. No more uvx, no
     per-client processes. Also clean up all dead code from the
     Whisper/Kokoro/OpenAI migration.

     Research Summary

     Docker: NOT VIABLE for audio on macOS

     - Docker Desktop/OrbStack runs containers in a Linux VM ‚ÄĒ no access to
     CoreAudio (mic/speakers)
     - No workaround is production-viable (PulseAudio over TCP adds 50-100ms
     latency, unreliable)
     - Decision: Run as a native process managed by launchd (macOS) or systemd
     (Linux)

     FastMCP HTTP Serving: ALREADY SUPPORTED

     - mcp.run(transport="http", host="0.0.0.0", port=8765) ‚ÄĒ starts Streamable
     HTTP server
     - Production: mcp.http_app() returns ASGI app for uvicorn
     - Server accessible at http://localhost:8765/mcp
     - VoiceMode already has a voicemode serve command that does this
     - No FastMCP 3.x upgrade needed ‚ÄĒ v2.x supports HTTP transport fully

     Tech Debt: 4 Critical, 10 High, 20 Medium/Low issues

     - Dead providers.py module (355 lines of OpenAI multi-provider routing)
     - Dead provider_discovery.py (vestigial abstraction)
     - Whisper/Kokoro tools still register with MCP server
     - converse.py has OpenAI client init, Kokoro auto-start, wrong model names
     - 30+ bare except: clauses
     - WHISPER_LANGUAGE used for ElevenLabs
     - openai still a core dependency

     Implementation Plan

     Phase 1: HTTP Server Setup (the core change)

     Step 1.1: Update MCP configs for HTTP transport

     Both .mcp.json (Claude) and mcp.json (Factory) change from stdio to URL:

     {
       "mcpServers": {
         "voicemode": {
           "type": "url",
           "url": "http://localhost:8765/mcp"
         }
       }
     }

     Step 1.2: Create launchd plist for auto-start

     File: ~/.voicemode/com.voicemode.server.plist (symlinked to
     ~/Library/LaunchAgents/)

     Must be a LaunchAgent (not Daemon) so it runs in the user session with
     audio access.

     <plist version="1.0">
     <dict>
         <key>Label</key><string>com.voicemode.server</string>
         <key>ProgramArguments</key>
         <array>
             <string>/Users/harsha/.local/bin/uv</string>
             <string>run</string>
             <string>--directory</string>
             <string>/Users/harsha/Developer/voicemode</string>
             <string>voicemode</string>
             <string>serve</string>
         </array>
         <key>WorkingDirectory</key><string>/Users/harsha/Developer/voicemode</s
     tring>
         <key>KeepAlive</key><true/>
         <key>StandardOutPath</key><string>/Users/harsha/.voicemode/logs/server.
     log</string>
         <key>StandardErrorPath</key><string>/Users/harsha/.voicemode/logs/serve
     r.err</string>
         <key>EnvironmentVariables</key>
         <dict>
             <key>PATH</key><string>/usr/local/bin:/opt/homebrew/bin:/usr/bin:/b
     in</string>
         </dict>
     </dict>
     </plist>

     Step 1.3: Add /start and /stop commands

     # Start
     launchctl load ~/Library/LaunchAgents/com.voicemode.server.plist

     # Stop
     launchctl unload ~/Library/LaunchAgents/com.voicemode.server.plist

     # Status
     launchctl list | grep voicemode

     Step 1.4: Verify voicemode serve works with current code

     The serve command already exists. Need to verify it works with ElevenLabs
     TTS/STT since the serve path may still use old OpenAI code.

     Files to check:
     - voice_mode/cli.py ‚ÄĒ the serve CLI command
     - voice_mode/serve_middleware.py ‚ÄĒ HTTP middleware
     - voice_mode/server.py ‚ÄĒ FastMCP server initialization

     Phase 2: Tech Debt ‚ÄĒ Critical Fixes

     Step 2.1: Fix providers.py broken function (C1)
     - get_preferred_voices() ‚Üí should be get_voice_preferences()
     - Or delete entire module (it's dead code)

     Step 2.2: Fix STT model name (C2)
     - model="whisper-1" ‚Üí model="scribe_v2" everywhere
     - Files: providers.py:186,204, converse.py:595,616

     Step 2.3: Remove dead AsyncOpenAI client creation (C3)
     - providers.py creates OpenAI clients for elevenlabs:// URLs ‚ÄĒ nonsensical
     - Either delete module or make it a thin ElevenLabs-only wrapper

     Step 2.4: Declare FFMPEG_AVAILABLE in config.py (C4)
     - Add FFMPEG_AVAILABLE = True to config.py (currently set dynamically by
     server.py)

     Phase 3: Tech Debt ‚ÄĒ High Priority Cleanup

     Step 3.1: Delete or gut dead modules
     - voice_mode/providers.py ‚ÄĒ 355 lines of dead OpenAI multi-provider routing
     - voice_mode/provider_discovery.py ‚ÄĒ vestigial abstraction
     (detect_provider_type always returns "elevenlabs")
     - voice_mode/openai_error_parser.py ‚ÄĒ OpenAI-specific error parsing

     ElevenLabs)

     management

     Step 3.2: Remove Whisper/Kokoro tools

     - voice_mode/tools/kokoro/ ‚ÄĒ 2 files (install, uninstall)

     - voice_mode/prompts/services.py ‚ÄĒ Whisper/Kokoro prompts
     - Remove whisper/kokoro sections from voice_mode/resources/configuration.py

     Step 3.3: Clean converse.py dead code
     - Remove from openai import AsyncOpenAI (line 16)
     - Remove openai_clients = get_openai_clients(...) (line 255)
     - Remove Kokoro auto-start in startup_initialization() (lines 260-311)
     - Remove get_tts_config() and get_stt_config() OpenAI mappers (lines
     317-381)
     - Update play_audio_feedback() to remove OpenAI params
     - Change model="whisper-1" to model="scribe_v2" (lines 595, 616)

     Step 3.4: Clean config.py legacy vars
     - Remove: PREFER_LOCAL, ALWAYS_TRY_LOCAL, AUTO_START_KOKORO
     - Remove: OPENAI_API_KEY (or make truly optional)
     - Update: TTS_VOICES default from "af_sky,alloy" to ElevenLabs voice ID
     - Update: TTS_MODELS default from "tts-1,tts-1-hd,gpt-4o-mini-tts" to
     "eleven_v3"
     - Update: TTS_SPEED comment from "0.25-4.0" to "0.7-1.2"
     - Rename: WHISPER_LANGUAGE ‚Üí STT_LANGUAGE
     - Remove: Whisper config section (model, port, language, model_path)
     - Remove: Kokoro config section (port, models_dir, cache_dir,
     default_voice, max_requests)
     - Update: reload_configuration() to remove Kokoro/Whisper URL fallbacks

     Step 3.5: Rename failover functions
     - elevenlabs_tts_stt.py: simple_tts_failover() ‚Üí elevenlabs_tts()
     - elevenlabs_tts_stt.py: simple_stt_failover() ‚Üí elevenlabs_stt()
     - Update all callers in converse.py and core.py

     Step 3.6: Clean shared.py
     - Remove Kokoro auto-start logic
     - Remove OpenAI cleanup
     - Simplify to ElevenLabs-only init/shutdown

     Step 3.7: Clean core.py
     - Remove get_openai_clients() function
     - Remove OpenAI TTS path in text_to_speech()
     - Remove cleanup() that closes OpenAI clients

     Step 3.8: Update pyproject.toml
     - Remove openai>=1.0.0 from core deps (or move to optional)
     - Remove aiohttp (was for Whisper/Kokoro installers)
     - Remove livekit and coreml optional extras
     - Update aiohttp comment
     - Remove livekit from keywords

     Phase 4: Tech Debt ‚ÄĒ Medium Priority

     Step 4.1: Add FastMCP Context to converse tool
     - Add ctx: Context parameter for progress reporting and structured logging

     Step 4.2: Fix bare except: clauses
     - Replace 30+ bare except: with specific exception types

     Step 4.3: Update MCP resources/docs
     - resources/docs/patterns.md, troubleshooting.md, parameters.md ‚ÄĒ replace
     OpenAI model references
     - resources/docs/minimal-tool-description.md ‚ÄĒ update for ElevenLabs

     Step 4.4: Update __init__.py docstring
     - Remove "Configurable OpenAI-compatible STT/TTS services"

     Execution Order

     1. Phase 1 first ‚ÄĒ get HTTP server running (Step 1.1-1.4)
     2. Phase 2 next ‚ÄĒ fix critical bugs (Step 2.1-2.4)

‚Źļ I see the issue. The on_session_started callback doesn't start the mic
  streaming ‚ÄĒ the mic streaming is started as a create_task at line 123, which
  fires immediately. But the event handlers are registered after the connection
  is created. The problem is a race condition: the SESSION_STARTED event could
  fire before the handlers are registered, and more critically, the mic
  streaming starts before the session is confirmed ready.

  Let me check the server logs from the failed second call:

  Searched for 1 pattern (ctrl+o to expand)

‚Źļ Found it. The second call at 17:14:43 connected but no session_started event 
  ever fired, and no mic capture log either. The WebSocket connected, but the
  session never started. The mic streaming task (_stream_microphone) was created
   but the session wasn't ready.

  The issue is that on the second call, the WebSocket connection succeeded but
  the ElevenLabs server never sent the session_started event. This could be
  because:

  1. The previous connection wasn't properly closed (ElevenLabs might rate-limit
   or reject)
  2. The connection is dangling from the first call

  Let me check if the connection close is clean:

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

‚Źļ I see two problems:

  1. Mic streaming starts before session_started ‚ÄĒ the mic task starts at line
  123 immediately, but should wait for SESSION_STARTED event
  2. No timeout on session start ‚ÄĒ if session_started never fires, the loop at
  line 127 just polls recording forever until max_duration (120s)

  The fix is to wait for session_started before starting mic streaming, and add
  a connection timeout. Let me also check how SuperWhisper and other reliable
  apps handle this ‚ÄĒ looking at the SDK's own example pattern:

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

‚Źļ The STT did work ‚ÄĒ it committed "Yeah yeah yeah I can hear" at 6.8s. But then
  when we tried to close the connection, the WebSocket close triggered an error
  event: sent 1000 (OK) User ended conversation; no close frame received. This
  error event set error_message, which caused the function to return
  connection_failed instead of the successful transcript.

  The bug is in the error handler ‚ÄĒ it treats the WebSocket close error as a
  real error, overwriting the committed text. The fix is to not set
  error_message if we already have committed text:

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

‚Źļ Update(voice_mode/elevenlabs_realtime_stt.py)

# Filesystem Provider                                                           
                                                                                
> Automatic component discovery from Python files                               
                                                                                
export const VersionBadge = ({version}) => {                                    
  return <Badge stroke size="lg" icon="gift" iconType="regular"                 
className="version-badge">                                                      
            New in version <code>{version}</code>                               
        </Badge>;                                                               
};                                                                              
                                                                                
<VersionBadge version="3.0.0" />                                                
                                                                                
`FileSystemProvider` scans a directory for Python files and automatically       
registers functions decorated with `@tool`, `@resource`, or `@prompt`. This     
enables a file-based organization pattern similar to Next.js routing, where     
your project structure becomes your component registry.                         
                                                                                
## Why Filesystem Discovery                                                     
                                                                                
Traditional FastMCP servers require coordination between files. Either your     
tool files import the server to call `@server.tool()`, or your server file      
imports all the tool modules. Both approaches create coupling that some         
developers prefer to avoid.                                                     
                                                                                
`FileSystemProvider` eliminates this coordination. Each file is                 
self-contained‚ÄĒit uses standalone decorators (`@tool`, `@resource`, `@prompt`)  
that don't require access to a server instance. The provider discovers these    
files at startup, so you can add new tools without modifying your server file.  
                                                                                
This is a convention some teams prefer, not necessarily better for all          
projects. The tradeoffs:                                                        
                                                                                
* **No coordination**: Files don't import the server; server doesn't import     
files                                                                           
* **Predictable naming**: Function names become component names (unless         
overridden)                                                                     
* **Development mode**: Optionally re-scan files on every request for rapid     
iteration                                                                       
                                                                                
## Quic                                                                         
‚Ä¶ +3525 lines ‚Ä¶                                                                 
hon  theme={"theme":{"light":"snazzy-light","dark":"dark-plus"}}                
from pathlib import Path                                                        
                                                                                
from fastmcp.server.providers.skills import SkillsDirectoryProvider             
                                                                                
provider = SkillsDirectoryProvider(                                             
    roots=Path.home() / ".claude" / "skills",                                   
    reload=True,                                                                
)                                                                               
```                                                                             
                                                                                
With `reload=True`, the provider re-discovers skills on each `list_resources()` 
 or `read_resource()` call. New skills appear, removed skills disappear, and    
modified content reflects current file state.                                   
                                                                                
<Warning>                                                                       
  Reload mode adds overhead to every request. Use it during development when    
you're actively editing skills, but disable it in production.                   
</Warning>                                                                      
                                                                                
## Client Utilities                                                             
                                                                                
FastMCP provides utilities for downloading skills from any MCP server that      
exposes them. These are standalone functions in `fastmcp.utilities.skills`.     
                                                                                
### Discovering Skills                                                          
                                                                                
Use `list_skills()` to see what skills are available on a server.               
                                                                                
```python  theme={"theme":{"light":"snazzy-light","dark":"dark-plus"}}          
from fastmcp import Client                                                      
from fastmcp.utilities.skills import list_skills                                
                                                                                
async with Client("http://skills-server/mcp") as client:                        
    skills = await list_skills(client)                                          
    for skill in skills:                                                        
        print(f"{skill.name}: {skill.description}")                             
```                                                                             
                                                                                
### Downloading Skills                                                          
                                                                                
Use `download_skill()` to download a single skill, or `sync_skills()` to        
download all available skills.                                                  
                                                                                
```python  theme={"theme":{"light":"snazzy-light","dark":"dark-plus"}}          
from pathlib import Path                                                        
                                                                                
from fastmcp import Client                                                      
from fastmcp.utilities.skills import download_skill, sync_skills                
                                                                                
async with Client("http://skills-server/mcp") as client:                        
    # Download one skill                                                        
    path = await download_skill(client, "pdf-processing", Path.home() /         
".claude" / "skills")                                                           
                                                                                
    # Or download all skills                                                    
    paths = await sync_skills(client, Path.home() / ".claude" / "skills")       
```                                                                             
                                                                                
Both functions accept an `overwrite` parameter. When `False` (default),         
existing skills are skipped. When `True`, existing files are replaced.          
                                                                                
### Inspecting Manifests                                                        
                                                                                
Use `get_skill_manifest()` to see what files a skill contains before            
downloading.                                                                    
                                                                                
```python  theme={"theme":{"light":"snazzy-light","dark":"dark-plus"}}          
from fastmcp import Client                                                      
from fastmcp.utilities.skills import get_skill_manifest                         
                                                                                
async with Client("http://skills-server/mcp") as client:                        
    manifest = await get_skill_manifest(client, "pdf-processing")               
    for file in manifest.files:                                                 
        print(f"{file.path} ({file.size} bytes, {file.hash})")                  
```
